Jamison Brereton

53 (407)
Maruts
┼Ъy─Бv─Бsva ─Аtreya
16 verses: kakubh 1, br╠еhat─л 2, anuс╣гс╣нubh 3, purau╠Ис╣гс╣Зih 4, kakubh 5, satobr╠еhat─л 6тАУ7, g─Бyatr─л 8, satobr╠еhat─л 9, kakubh 10тАУ11, g─Бyatr─л 12, satobr╠еhat─л 13тАУ14, kakubh 15, satobr╠еhat─л 16
A metrically complex hymn, though there is no reason to consider it a composite. The internal groupings, mostly two-verse units, follow those suggested by Oldenberg (1888: 106тАУ8). The hymn mingles descriptions of and wishes for the MarutsтАЩ jour ney here with descriptions of the storm and the desirable rain the Maruts bring, and indeed the Maruts and the rains are sometimes identified, sometimes modulate from one to the other.

The hymn opens (vss. 1тАУ2), as often, with questionsтАФwhat is the origin of Maruts and where have they gone? The Maruts themselves answer, indirectly, in verse 3, and demand praise, which is forthcoming in verse 4. The description of a storm follows (vss. 5тАУ7), and the Maruts are urged to come here with their rains (vss. 8тАУ11). The poet returns in verses 12тАУ13 to the question raised at the begin
ning: to what sacrificer have the Maruts gone? The hope is of course that they have come or will come to us, and the blessings we wish to receive are detailed in the final verses (14тАУ16.)

Jamison Brereton Notes

Maruts For the complex metrical structure of the hymn, see published introduction. Despite the numerous different names for the meters, with few meters repeated in adjacent vss., they are all combinations of 8- and 12-syllable p─Бdas, and so the hymns is metrically more harmonious than the long list of meters implies.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho knows the birth of these (Maruts)? who has formerly been (participant) of the enjoyments of them (by whom) the spotted deer are harnessed (to their chariots)?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who knows their birth? Or, who was previously in the graces of the Maruts,
when they yoked their own spotted (female antelopes)?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like V.52.14 in the immediately preceding hymn, this vs. contains a v─Б тАШorтАЩ whose disjunctive alternatives do not seem parallel. While it is true that both alternatives are questions beginning with k├бс╕е тАШwhoтАЩ, the questions seem ill-matched.

RenouтАЩs assessment here is тАЬillogisme de v─Б╠Б[sic – he prints it with accent].тАЭ Perhaps the point is that if no one knows as far back as the MarutsтАЩ birth, there may still be someone who has had long association with them and their habits.

Griffith

Who knows the birth of these, or who lived in the Maruts’ favour in the days of old
What time their spotted deer were yoked?

Geldner

Wer kennt den Ursprung? Oder wer war fr├╝her in der Marut Gunst, wenn sie ihre Schecken angeschirrt haben?

Grassmann

Wer ist’s, der ihren Ursprung kennt? wer ist zuvor gewesen in der Maruts Huld, Als sie die Schecken sich geschirrt?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho has head them, when standing in their cars, (declare) whither they go? Upon what liberal worshipper do their kindred rains descend together with manifold food?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those mounted on their chariotsтАФwho heard (them)? How did
they drive?
Toward what good giver, (what) friend, did they flow along (as) friends, (as) rains (flow) with their refreshments?

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b kath─Б╠Бyayuс╕е could be resolved as kath─Б╠Б─Б╠Бyayuс╕е тАЬhow did they drive here?тАЭ This interpr. might be favored by ─Бyay├║с╕е in 3a, although it is disfavored by pr├б yayuс╕е in 12b.

The sandhi form ─Бp├бya at the end of c is universally interpr. as the nom. pl.

─Бp├бyaс╕е, referring to the Maruts; it could, however, be just as easily dat. sg. ─Бp├бye and refer to the good giver (sud─Б╠Бse) immediately preceding. In fact, I think it should be read as both, as reflected in the published translation This double reading is favored by the way the vs. is structured, a striking pattern discovered by Natalie Operstein (in class, early 2000s). In general in this verse syntactic constituency is alternating and interlocked – that is, constituents have the pattern X Y XтАЩ YтАЩ, etc. So, p─Бda a: ─Б╠Б r├бtheс╣гu et─Б╠Бn tasth├║с╣гaс╕е with the acc. pl. et─Б╠Бn тАж tasth├║с╣гaс╕е interrupted by the loc. pl. r├бtheс╣гu, which is governed by ─Б╠Бpreceding the acc. pl. The pattern is similar in cd: k├бsmai sud─Б╠Бse ├нс╕Н─Бbhir sah├б sasruс╕е ├бnv vr╠ес╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е ─Бp├бya The datives k├бsmai тАж sud─Б╠Бse form a constituent, interrupted by the 3rd pl. verb sasruс╕е, whose preverb ├бnu follows the dat. sud─Б╠Бse and whose overt subj., nom. pl.

vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е itself interrupts the postpositional phrase ├нс╕Н─Бbhiс╕е тАж sah├б. In this configuration ─Бp├бya is not definitively paired: it could go with dat. sud─Б╠Бse, separated from it by the prev. ├бnu, or with the nom. pl. vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е, likewise separated from it by a single word, instr. ├нd─Бbhiс╕е. Note also that it is the final word of a 12-syllable p─Бda, in a verse whose other p─Бdas are 8-syllables, so it is metrically almost isolated and could almost (not quite – itтАЩs only 3 syllables) attach itself to d rather than c. Since ─Бp├н- тАШfriendтАЩ is an inherently receiprocal word, its double application is especially appropriate.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo me have they spoken; they have come to me with radiant steeds to (drink) the exhilarating beverage; to them (they have said), when, beholding them, who are the formless leaders (of rites), and friends of man, repeat our prais.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Formless: arepasaс╕е alepa = intangible

Jamison Brereton

They say to meтАФthose who drove hither through the days along with the birds, in exuberance,
the men, unblemished young bloods: тАЬWhen you see them here,
praise them!тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The referent of t├й in the opening phrase t├й ma ─Бhuс╕е тАЬThey say to meтАЭ is not entirely clear. It is universally taken as the Maruts, and that is probably correct.

Among other things it is reminiscent of the MarutsтАЩ proclamations тАЬto meтАЭ in the previous hymn: 52.10 тАж m├бhyam тАж ohate and 52.16 тАж me тАж v├│canta. However, it is possible that the subj. is instead unidentified human associates of the poet. This would avoid the awkwardness of having the Maruts refer to themselves in the 3rd ps.: тАЬThey say to me, тАШWhen you see them [expect тАЬusтАЭ], praise.тАЩтАЭ In p─Бda a note the figure ─Бhur y├б ─Бyay├║r. As Renou points out, y├б ─Бyayuс╕е тАж m├бde is the implicit answer to kath─Б╠Бyayuс╕е in 1b. The two instr. in b dy├║bhir v├нbhiс╕е have provoked more commentary than they probably deserve. Geldner (fld by Witzel Got┼Н) takes the former as referring to daybreak and the birds are then the birds that start stirring at that time. This is not impossible, but dy├║bhiс╕е (incl. ├║pa dy├║bhiс╕е VIII.40.8) generally means тАШthrough the days, day after dayтАЩ, and that is fine here. The Maruts would then fly тАЬwith the birdsтАЭ because they come through the midspace, where birds are at home.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The praise of them) who are all self-irradiating splendid in ornaments, in arms, in garlands, in breast-plural tes, in bracelets, in chariots, in bows.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In bracelets: kh─Бdiс╣гu; in an earlier text kh─Бdi = hasta tranaka, a guard for the hand or arm (RV. 1.23.43); here, it is explained as: hastap─Бdasthita kaс╣нah─Бс╕е = rings for the hands or feet,bracelets or anklets

Jamison Brereton

Who in their unguents, who in their axes have their own radianceтАФand in their garlands, in their brilliants, in their spangles,
with splendor in their chariots, in their bows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. consists entirely of a nominal rel. cl. without verb, presumably hanging off vs. 3.

The problematic form is the hapax ┼Ыr─Бy─Б╠Б(Pp. ┼Ыr─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е). It is generally taken as a nom. pl. thematic deriv. of тИЪ┼Ыri, so тАШresting inтАЩ, attenuated by some to тАШprovided withтАЩ (with loc.). I cannot find particular fault with this analysis, save for its banality and the unclear source of the root-syllable ─Б. I am inclined instead to take it as an instr. sg. (┼Ыr─Бy─Б╠Б, equally possible in this sandhi situation) to a derivative of тИЪ┼Ыr─л, parallel to ┼Ыriy─Б╠Б, which is regularly used of the Maruts. But I confess I do not know why ┼Ыriy─Б╠БwouldnтАЩt have been used instead or exactly what the derivational mechanism would be, incl. again the source of the vс╣Ыddhi.

Who shine self-luminous with ornaments and swords, with breastplates, armlets, and with wreaths,
Arrayed on chariots and with bows.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI contemplate your chariots, munificent Maruts, with delight, like wandering lights in the rains.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It is following your chariots (when they come) that I take my place for delight, you Maruts of lively drops [/lively gifts],
(I delighting) like the heavens (following the waters) when they come with their rain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The construction of this vs. is very problematic and has been much discussed (see, e.g., OldenbergтАЩs long consideration). In the end my interpr. is closest, but not identical, to RenouтАЩs, though perhaps not arrived at by the same means.

To deal with the easiest issue first, pace Grassmann and Geldner I do not construe ├бnu тАж dadhe together. For one thing ├бnu тИЪdh─Б barely exists; moreover a preverb in tmesis is unlikely to move to the end of the preceding p─Бda (so also Renou). Rather, it surely governs preceding immediately r├бth─Бn, like similarly p─Бda-final r├│das─л ├бnu in 6c. It can be further noted that ├бnu is a signature word of this hymn, occurring 6x: 2c, 5a, 6c, 10c, 11c, 16c. With ├бnu otherwise assigned, the simplex verb dadhe тАШI take my placeтАЩ is then easily construed with the purpose dat. mud├й.

The real problem in the verse is what to do with p─Бda c. The easy sense that Geldner extracts from it (тАЬdie wie die Himmel (Tage) mit Regen kommenтАЭ) makes a hash of the grammar. Assuming that he means dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е to be compared with the chariots, with the point of comparison found in the part. тАШcomingтАЩ (yat─л╠Бс╕е), 1) dy─Б╠Бvah must be taken as an acc., which is simply impossible; or 2) the alternative to 1) is to assume the whole simile has reverted to the nominative, something that doesnтАЩt happen in RV, as I long ago demonstrated (тАЬCase disharmonyтАжтАЭ) though Geldner asserts it here (his n. 5c referring to his n. to I.180.3d); 3) the fem. part. yat─л╠Бс╕е should modify masc. r├бth─Бn or else, by attraction, dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е, which latter is only fem. in the meaning тАШheavenтАЩ, not тАШdayтАЩ.

A way to a solution (or partial solution) comes from recognizing that the fem.

pl. part. yat─л╠Бс╕е regularly modifies тАШwatersтАЩ; cf. ─Б╠Бpaс╕е n├б prav├бt─Б yat─л╠Бс╕е VIII.6.34 = 13.8 = IX.24.2, ─Б╠Бpo ├бdс╣Ы┼Ыram ─Бyat─л╠Бс╕е X.30.13, ap─Б╠Бm ├бrthaс╣Г yat─л╠Бn─Бm. It is therefore quite likely, esp. in this rainy context, that тАШwatersтАЩ is gapped here, solving the gender problem – and also the case problem, because, adding another nominal element to the syntagm allows dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е to take its expected nominative role and respond to the acc. represented by (ap├│) yat─л╠Бс╕е. RenouтАЩs tr. reflects this: тАЬcomme les cieux (agr├йent les eaux), qui vont avec la pluie.тАЭ The question is then what is the mediating verb? RenouтАЩs тАШagr├йentтАЩ makes sense, but he doesnтАЩt explain where he got it. I think it is possible to generate it from the datival mud├й of b, either by simply switching emphasis from the finite verb dadhe to its infinitval complement or, in a trickier move, reading mud├й a 2nd time, but this time as a 1st sg. mid. to a root present: тИЪmud has a hapax med. root opt. mud─лmahi, and though it is generally classified as a root aor., a root pres. is certainly not excluded. It is worth noting that this opt. is construed with the preverb ├бnu (VIII.1.14 ├бnu st├│mam mudh─лmahi). Assuming this lexeme in our c would simplify the rendering of the simile. I therefore suggest a slight alteration to the published translation, to тАЬ(I delighting/delight) like the heavens (in the waters) when they come with their rain.тАЭ See also disc. ad 10c, which in some ways repairs this problematic passage.

Griffith

O swift to pour your bounties down, ye Maruts, with delight I look upon your cars,
Like splendours coming through the rain.

Geldner

Eure Wagen ben├╢tige ich zur Freude, o raschspendende Marut, die wie die Himmel mit Regen kommen.

Grassmann

Ich rege eure Wagen an zur Wonne mir, o tropfenreiche Marutschar, Wie Blitze die durch Regen gehn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLeaders (of the rain), munificent givers, they cause that which is the treasury (of water) to fall from the sky for (the benefit of) the donor (of the offering); they let loose the rain cloud, and the shedders of rain spread (everywhere) with (abundant) water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the men of good drops [/gifts] have stirred the bucket of heaven here for the one doing pious work,
they send the thunder(storm) surging out along the two world-halves; along the wasteplaces come the rains.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted by most comm., masc. acc. sg. y├бm, presumably modifying k├│┼Ыam, has no referent in the main cl. Such тАЬimproperтАЭ relativization is not rare in the RV.

├бnu at the end of c can also, secondarily, be read with d: ├бnu, dh├бnvan─Б.

Griffith

Munificent Heroes, they have cast heaven’s treasury down for the worshipper’s behoof:
They set the storm-cloud free tostream through both the worlds, and rainfloods flow o’er desert spots.

Geldner

Wenn die gabensch├╢nen Herren f├╝r den Opferspender des Himmels Eimer heraufgezogen haben, so lassen sie den Parjanya ├╝ber beide Welten sich ergie├Яen. Des Parjanya Str├╢me gehen ├╝ber das trockene Land.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gliding (torrents), issuing (from the clouds), overspread the firmament with water, as cows (yield milk), and like rapid horses let loose upon the road, the rivers rush in various directions.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The rivers, having bored with their gush through the dusky realm, have flowed forth like milk-cows,
like horses that have streamed from the road at their unharnessing, when the dappled females turn aside.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In c I construe ├бdhvanaс╕е as an abl. with syann─Б╠Б(с╕е) rather than a gen. with vim├│cane. The effective difference is trivial, but the image seems more dynamic if the horses, unhitched, rush off into the roadside pastures (perhaps in pursuit of the тАЬdappled females,тАЭ though if the latter are antelopes, this would lead to species crossbreeding).

Griffith

The bursting streams m billowy flood have spread abroad, like milch-kine, o’er the firmament.
Like swift steeds hasting to their journey’s resting-place, to every side run glittering brooks.

Geldner

Die freigemachten Str├╢me ergossen sich mit ihrer Flut in den Luftraum wie K├╝he, wie Rosse am Ende des Weges laufend, wenn ihre Schecken vom Wege abbiegen.

Grassmann

Die Str├╢me, die mit Fluten drangen durch die Luft, ergossen sich den K├╝hen gleich, Wie Hengste tr├дufelnd, wenn vom Wege heimgekehrt, sie zu den bunten Stuten gehn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome, Maruts, from heaven, from the firmament, or from this (earth); tarry not far off.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Drive hither, Maruts, from heaven, from the midspace, and from nearby.
Do not stay away at a distance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The abl. par─Бv├бtaс╕е is somewhat odd with m─Б╠Бva sth─Бta тАЬdonтАЩt stay awayтАЭ; we would expect loc. par─Бv├бti, which is quite well-attested. It may be that par─Бv├бtaс╕е has simply been harmonized with the ablatives in ab: div├б(с╕е) тАж ant├бrikс╣г─Бd am─Б╠Бt.

However, itтАЩs also possible to take m─Б╠Бva sth─Бta in c as a parenthetical exclamation and par─Бv├бtaс╕е as a continuation of the abl. phrase of ab: тАЬDrive hither, Maruts, from heaven, from the midspace, from nearby – donтАЩt stay away! – and from a distance.тАЭ This might also explain the unusual p─Бda-final ut├б of b. I therefore offer this as an alternative to the published translation

There is also the question of what the lexeme ├бva тИЪsth─Б means here.

Generally it means тАШdescendтАЩ, often into a river or the like (see Renou ad loc.). But that doesnтАЩt make sense here: if the Maruts are to come here from heaven or the midspace, as they are invited to in ab, they will have to descend. If we take the ├бva seriously, perhaps the idea is that the Maruts shouldnтАЩt perform their descent somewhere else than here– at a distance – perhaps into the rivers named in the next vs. But this seems overly complex.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological modulation of #─Б╠Б… (8a) to #m─Б╠Бva…(8c) to #m─Б╠Бvo (9a) / m─Б╠Бvaс╕е (9bc). The vaс╕е then migrates to the end of 9d.

Griffith

Hither, O Maruts, come from heaven, from mid-air, or from near at hand
Tarry not far away from us.

Geldner

Kommt her, ihr Marut, vom Himmel, von der Luft und von daheim; ziehet nicht ab in die Fernen!

Grassmann

Vom Himmel kommt, o Maruts her, aus weiter Luft, von nahem Ort, nicht bleibet in der Ferne stehn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet not the Rasa, the Anitabh─Б, the Kubh─Б, or the wide-roving ocean delay you; let not the watery Sarayu oppose you; may the happiness of your (approach) be ours.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rasa, Anitabh─Б, Kubh─Б: names of rivers; the wide-roving ocean: kramuс╕е sindhuс╕е = sarvatra kramaс╣Зaс╕е samudra, the every-where going ocean

Jamison Brereton

Let not the Ras─Б (River), the Anitabh─Б, the Kubh─Б, the Krumu, let not the Sindhu bring you to a halt.
Let not the overflowing Sarayu hem you around. On us alone let your favor be. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
08-09 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological modulation of #─Б╠Б… (8a) to #m─Б╠Бva…(8c) to #m─Б╠Бvo (9a) / m─Б╠Бvaс╕е (9bc). The vaс╕е then migrates to the end of 9d.

Griffith

So let not Rasa, Krumu, or Anitabha, Kubha, or Sindhu hold you back.
Let not the watery Sarayti obstruct your way. With us be all the bliss ye give.

Geldner

Nicht soll euch die Rasa, Anitabha, Kubha, Krumu, nicht euch die Sindhu aufhalten, noch euch die quellenreiche Sarayu im Wege stehen. Bei uns soll eure Huld sein.

Grassmann

Nicht halt euch Rasa, Kubha noch Anitubha, nicht Krumu noch die Sindhu auf; Nicht hemme euch die wasserreiche Saraju; bei uns allein sei eure Lust.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬI praise that brilliant company of the Maruts, who have your strength of recent chariots, you whom the rains attend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your troop of chariots, the glittering Marut flock of newer (тАЬhymnsтАЭ [=thunderclaps])
do the rains come following after.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In some ways this vs. is both a variant and a repair of vs. 5. Like that vs. it begins with an acc. phrase referring to the MarutsтАЩ chariots. Following (├бnu) them come the rains: ├бnu pr├б yanti vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е, a variant of 5c vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─л╠БтАж yat─л╠Бr iva тАЬ(fem. pl. ) coming with their rain,тАЭ where I supplied тАШwatersтАЩ as the referent of the participle.

The syntax is somewhat different, but the elements are there. In this passage the relationship between the metaphor and the natural world is drawn more clearly: the chariots and the flock of Maruts represent thunder and lightning (see below), which are regularly followed by rain.

While a, c may function as repair, the phrase in b, тАж gaс╣З├бm m─Б╠Бrutam n├бvyas─лn─Бm, introduces a new poetic complication. It is found identically in V.58.1, where it is even more troublesome. The problem is what to supply with gen. pl. fem.

n├бvyas─лn─Бm. Geldner and Renou, rather bizarrely, choose to supply Maruts – e.g., Geldner тАЬder тАж marutische Schar der neuesten (Marut).тАЭ This not only contravenes the unmistakable gender of n├бvyas─лn─Бm, but it produces an awkward and clunky pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ expression.

It is also unclear to me who the тАЬnewerтАЭ or тАЬnewestтАЭ (latter both Geldner and Renou) Maruts would be: it is generally emphasized that the Maruts are indistinguishable and тАЬthere is no last oneтАЭ (V.58.5). Nonetheless the view that n├бvyas─лn─Бm refers to the Maruts is well entrenched. There is no masc. gen. pl. comparative attested in Vedic, and both Lanman (Noun Inflec. 515) and Macdonell (VG 234) state that the fem. form is used instead in these two passages тАЬin agreement with mar├║t─БmтАЭ (Macdonell, as if gen. pl.

mar├║t─Бm were actually in the passage), due to тАЬmetrical exigenciesтАЭ (again Macdonell, but same view expressed by Lanman). The metrical argument is strikingly weak: although neither a putative masc. gen. pl. *n├бvyas─Бm nor *n├бv─лyas─Бm built to the alternative comparative stem would fit this exact metrical slot even with distraction of the gen. pl. ending (as here), neither form would have any trouble fitting into other parts of a Vedic metrical line, and itтАЩs difficult to believe that a poet like ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva would set his heart on putting a comparative just here and then seriously distort the grammar to shove it in. (S─Бyaс╣Зa., it should be noted, does not supply Maruts, but still ignores the gender of n├бvyas─лn─Бm by glossing it with the grammatically ambiguous n┼лtan─Бn─Бm and then connecting that gen. pl. with r├бth─Бn─Бm in p─Бda a.) Witzel Got┼Н have the merit of supplying a fem., namely тАШrainsтАЩ, borrowed from the vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е of c. But this again seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++: why would the rains follow the rains, and indeed why would the (temporally unmarked) rains follow the newer rains? I start by considering what is regularly called тАШnewerтАЩ. To this there is a ready answer: hymns, songs, formulations, thoughts, etc. – the standard verbal products celebrated in RVic discourse, several of which are fem. In fact, note that in the next vs. (53.11) two such words are prominently positioned at the ends of p─Бdas: su┼Ыast├нbhiс╕е (11b) тАШgood chantsтАЩ and dh─лt├нbhiс╕е (11c) тАШpoetic thoughtsтАЩ, both of which are elsewhere modified by n├бvyas─л-: VIII.5.25 n├бvyas─лbhiс╕е su┼Ыast├нbhiс╕е; I.143.1 … n├бvyas─лс╣Г dh─лt├нm.

I therefore propose that we should supply such a word with n├бvyas─лn─Бm in 10b. (In the published translation it is тАШhymnsтАЩ.) But this produces an odd locution, тАЬthe Marut flock of newer (hymns),тАЭ with semantically ill-assorted elements joined – or so it seems at first glance. But remember that the poet is depicting a metaphorical thunderstorm: the rains, undisguised, come last, but I think we have both thunder and lightning earlier in the vs.: the flock is tveс╣г├бm тАШglitteringтАЩ (though, I must admit, the word sometimes just means тАШturbulentтАЩ: see v─Б╠Бta-tviс╣г- тАШturbulent as the windтАЩ in the next hymn, V.54.3), which can represent the lightning. And the flock also consists of тАЬhymns,тАЭ which in this context can be the regular booming of thunder claps.

English translation:

тАЬLet us wait with sacred praises and holy rites upon your several strength, and separate troop, and individual company.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your every troop of these (chariots), every swarm, every flock, with good chants
we would stride after, with poetic thoughts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The MarutsтАЩ thunder-hymns are then met with our reciprocal offered praise hymns.

In p─Бda a va eс╣г─Бm is taken by all standard tr. as a doubled gen. pl., essentially тАЬof these you,тАЭ though not so tr. I think rather that eс╣г─Бm refers to the chariots, and vaс╕е is the gen. dependent on the whole NP ┼Ы├бrdhaс╣Г-┼Ыardham тАж eс╣г─Бm, which simply reprises 10a t├бс╣Г vaс╕е ┼Ы├бrdhaс╣Г r├бth─Бn─Бm, with gen. pl. of the chariots.

Griffith

With eulogies and hymns may we follow your army, troop by troop, and band by band,
And company by company.

Geldner

Jeden Heerhaufen von euch, jedes Geschwader, jeden Trupp wollen wir mit Lobpreisungen, mit frommen Gedanken begleiten.

Grassmann

Drum wollen wir euch Schar f├╝r Schar und Trupp f├╝r Trupp und Schwarm f├╝r Schwarm mit Lobgesang, Und mit Gebeten schreiten nach.

English translation:

тАЬTo what well-born and oblation-giving (worshipper) will the Maruts today in tthis their car?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To what well-born one, who had given an oblation, have they driven forth today
along this courseтАФthe Maruts?

Jamison Brereton Notes

The question k├бsmai тАж pr├б yayuс╕е тАЬto whom have they drivenтАЭ returns us to the questions in vs. 2: kath─Б╠Бyayuс╕е / k├бsmai sasruс╕е тАЬHow have they driven? To whom have they flowed?тАЭ The referent of k├бsmai in 2, the тАЬgood giverтАЭ (sud─Б╠Бse), is further specified here as тАЬone who has given an oblationтАЭ (r─Бt├бhavy─Бya), though with different roots тАШgiveтАЩ. This ring-compositional reprise brings to a close the descriptive portion of the hymn, and the poet turns to requests.

Griffith

To what oblation-giver, sprung of noble ancestry, have sped
The Maruts on this course to-day?

Geldner

Zu welchem edelgeborenen Opferspender haben sich heute die Marut auf dieser Fahrt begeben,

Grassmann

Zu welchem hochgeborenen, der Opfer spendet, drangen heut Auf ihrer Fahrt die Maruts vor?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith the same (goodwill) that you bestow imperishable grain-seed upon a son or grandson, bestow it upon us, for we ask of you life-sustaining and auspicious wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Imperishable grain-seed: dh─Бnyam b─лjam akс╣гitam: unperishing grain-seed

Jamison Brereton

тАФAlong which (course) you convey the imperishable granular seed to offspring and descendants.
Establish for us what we implore you for: generosity through our whole lifetime and good fortune.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With the standard tr. I take y├йna in p─Бda as referring to en─Б╠Бy─Б╠Бmena in the previous vs. (12c).

I tr. dh─Бny├а- lit., тАШrelated to grain (dh─Бn─Б╠Б), as тАШgranularтАЩ, because I think it refers both to the raindrops, shaped like grain, and the actual grain that results from the rain.

I.57.1 r─Б╠Бdho v├н┼Ыv─Б╠Бyu suggests that vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бyu belongs to what precedes, rather than to sa├║bhagam as Geldner and Renou take it.

Griffith

Vouchsafe to us the bounty, that which we implore, through which, for child and progeny,
Ye give the seed of corn that wasteth not away, and bliss that reacheth to all life.

Geldner

Mit der ihr f├╝r leiblichen Nachwuchs das unversiegliche Saatkorn bringt? Gew├дhret uns die Gabe, um die wir euch bitten, um Gl├╝ck f├╝r das ganze Leben!

Grassmann

Den Schatz gew├дhrt uns, den, um welchen wir euch flehn, durch den f├╝r Kind und Enkel ihr Getreidesamen bringet, unverg├дnglichen, das Gl├╝ck, das alles Leben schafft.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдореИрдГ рдЕрд╡рджреНрдпрдВ рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрдЬреНрдп рдирд┐рджрдГ рдирд┐рдиреНрджрдХрд╛рдиреН рдЕрд░рд╛рддреАрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рддрд┐рд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдиреН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рддрд┐рд░рдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐рддрдореН ред рдЕрддреАрдпрд╛рдо рдЕрддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореНрдп рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдо рддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдХреБрд░реНрдо рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдиреЗрдирд╛рдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдд рдЙрддреНрддрд░реЗрдгреЗрд╖реНрдЯрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд░реБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реА рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╖реБ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрдкреНрд░реЗрд░рд┐рддрд╛рд╕реБ рд╕рддреАрд╖реБ рд╢рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдпреЛрдГ рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рд╡рдирдВ рдЪ рдЖрдкрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рее рд╢рд╕рдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдЬрд╕реН рее рдЙрд╕реНрд░рд┐ рдЧреЛрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рднреЗрд╖рдЬрдореН ред рдпрджреНрдпрдкреНрдпреЗрддрджреБрджрдХрдирд╛рдо рддрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рдкреГрдердЧрдкрд╛рдорднрд┐рдзрд╛рдирд╛рджрддреНрд░ рддрджреНрдзреЗрддреБрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдордиреНрдирдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╣ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рд▓рднреЗрдорд╣рд┐ рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╡рдпрдореН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЖрдкреЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрдкреНрд░реЗрд░рд┐рддрд╛ рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╕рд╣реИрд╡ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рднрд╡реЗрдо рдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрд╕реНрд╡рднреВрддрд╛рдГ рее

English translation:

тАЬMay we overcomeour secret and reviling adversaries, having departed from iniquity by good deeds; may we possess, Maruts, through the rain (sent by you), unmixed happiness, water, cattle and herbs.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May we cross over beyond scorners through your blessings, having left behind imperfection and hostilities.
When it rains, the waters are luck and lifetime; at dawn they are
medicine. May we be together with (them/you), o Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take usr├н as having temporal domain over the whole of p─Бda c: тАЬwhen it rains, the waters at dawn are luck, lifetime, and medicine.тАЭ I donтАЩt see any way to tell, and in fact I donтАЩt see why dawn should limit any of these predicates.

Griffith

May we in safety pass by those who slander us, leaving behind disgrace and hate.
Maruts, may we be there when ye, at dawn, in rest and toil, rain waters down and balm.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддреЛ ! рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рдирд┐рджреЛрд╜рддреАрдпрд╛рдо рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд╕реНрддрд┐рд░реЛрд╜рд╡рджреНрдпрдорд░рд╛рддреАрд╢реНрдЪ рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рдВ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реА рдЖрдкреЛ рдпреЛрд░реБрд╕реНрд░рд┐ рднреЗрд╖рдЬрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рддрдерд╛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрднрд╡рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрддрд┐, рдЗрдпрд╛рдо) рдЙрд▓реНрд▓рдЩреНрдШреЗрдо рддреНрдпрдЬреЗрдо (рдирд┐рджрдГ) рдпреЗ рдирд┐рдиреНрджрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН рдорд┐рдереНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдирдГ (рддрд┐рд░рдГ) рддрд┐рд░рд╢реНрдЪреАрдирдВ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдо (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ (рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреНрдпрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ (рдЕрд╡рджреНрдпрдореН) рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд┐рддрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо (рдЕрд░рд╛рддреАрдГ) рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН (рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реА) рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ (рд╢рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рдпреЛрдГ) рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдореН (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рдЙрд╕реНрд░рд┐) рдЧрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рднреЗрд╖рдЬрдореН) рдФрд╖рдзрдореН (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╕рд╣) реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрдирд┐рдиреНрджрдХрд╛рдиреН рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рдкрд┐рдирдГ рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рдЪ рддреНрдпрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рддреНрдпреМрд╖рдзрд╛рджрд┐рд╕реЗрд╡рдиреЗрди рд╢рд░реАрд░рдорд░реЛрдЧрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕реЗрдирд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдореБрдиреНрдиреАрдп рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдорд╛рдкреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН реерезрекрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

mortal be

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraise the givers of enjoyment, (the Maruts), at the sacrifice of this worshiper, (for they) delight in (pious praise) like cattle in fodder; wherefore call upon them as if upon friends; praise them, desirous of praise, with a sacred hymn.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise the benefactors of the praiser on the journey of this (flock). They will take pleasure as cows do in a pasture.
Invoke them as they go, like old comrades. With song sing (to) those who desire it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Unaccented asya should not modify stuvat├бс╕е as Witzel Got┼Н take it. Better the solutions of Geldner and Renou, esp. the latter, who separate these two genitives, with Renou supplying тАЬMarut troopтАЭ with asya.

Griffith

Praise the Free-givers. At this liberal patron’s rite they joy like cattle in the mead.
So call thou unto them who come as ancient Friends: hymn those who love thee with a song.

Geldner

Preise die Wohlt├дter des Preisenden auf dessen Fahrt; sie sollen sich behagen wie die K├╝he auf der Weide. Ruf ihnen nach wie alten Freunden, wenn sie gehen, lobe sie mit Lobrede, die das lieben!

Grassmann

Die Geber preise, m├╢gen bei des S├дngers Fest wie K├╝h’ im Grase schwelgen sie, Wie alte Freunde ruf die Fahrenden du an, mit Lied erfreu die l├╝sternen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рд░рдгрдБрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рддреЛ рднреЛрдЬрд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрддреБрд╣рд┐ред рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдпрд╛рдордирд┐ рдпрддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рд╡ рд╕рдЦреАрдиреН рдЧрд┐рд░рд╛рд╜рдиреБ рд╣реНрд╡рдп рд╕рдЦреАрдиреН рдпрд╡рд╕реЗ рдЧрд╛рд╡реЛ рдирд╛рд╜рдиреБ рд╣реНрд╡рдп рдХрд╛рдорд┐рдиреЛ рдЧреГрдгреАрд╣рд┐ реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реНрддреБрд╣рд┐) (рднреЛрдЬрд╛рдиреН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдиреН (рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдХрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╕реНрдп (рдпрд╛рдордирд┐) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗ (рд░рдгрдиреН) рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢рдиреН (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдпрд╡рд╕реЗ) рдмреБрд╕рд╛рджреМ (рдпрддрдГ) (рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рд╡) рдпрдерд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реНрддрдерд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН (рд╕рдЦреАрдиреН) рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН (рдЕрдиреБ) (рд╣реНрд╡рдп) рдирд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдп (рдЧрд┐рд░рд╛) рд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛ (рдЧреГрдгреАрд╣рд┐) (рдХрд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдВ рдХрд╛рдореЛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдорд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд╣реГрджрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрдХрд╛рдорд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ реерезремрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╢реНрдиреЛрддреНрддрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛! рдЬреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп, рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдЕрд╕реВрди рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреА рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реЗ рдЕрд╕рддреАрд▓ рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░. рее резрем рее
